## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and temperature modifies material stiffness, yield strength, and flow behavior through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood type plastic hardening)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating strain hardening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with temperature dependence)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Temperature-dependent Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with Arrhenius thermal factor)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Thermally-activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow law: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)
- Linear thermal + power hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (modulus linear in T with hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperature → multiplicative factor exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*T) on stress
- Strain hardening saturation → terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating approach to ultimate stress
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 for work-hardening metals
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield before hardening term
- Coupled thermo-mechanical behavior → product structure f(epsilon)*g(T) indicating separable strain and temperature contributions
- Pre-strain or reference strain offset → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c/T) factor indicating thermally-activated dislocation motion
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → piecewise or smooth transition like tanh(c*epsilon) blending linear and nonlinear regimes

1. `T*c*epsilon**3` (linear in T times epsilon^3)
2. `c*epsilon**3` (constant times epsilon^3)
3. `c*epsilon**0.1998*exp(-c/T)` (epsilon^~0.2 times exp(-const/T))

The critical term is `exp(-c/T)`. Note that `epsilon**0.1998 ≈ epsilon**(1/5)`.

Now I need to find candidates with `exp(-c/T)` or equivalent. Let me check:

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c1*epsilon**(1/5) + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4*epsilon**(1/3)*exp(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*exp(c8/T) + c9/T`

This has `c7*exp(c8/T)`. Setting c8 to a negative value gives `exp(-|c8|/T)`. But this term doesn't have `epsilon**(1/5)` multiplied with it. The `epsilon**(1/5)` term is separate (`c1*epsilon**(1/5)`). The GT needs `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T)` combined. Here they're separate, so this can't match unless we can somehow combine them, which we can't since they're additive terms.

Let me look for candidates with a term like `epsilon**c * exp(something/T)` or `epsilon**c * exp(T*c)` where `T*c` could approximate `-c/T` — no, that's impossible.

**Candidate 8:** `T*T**c0*c1*epsilon**c2 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + c4 + c5*epsilon**3 + c6*exp(c7*epsilon**c8) + c9*epsilon**c2`

The term `T*T**c0 = T**(1+c0)`. If c0 = -1, this becomes constant. Not helpful for matching `exp(-c/T)`.

Going back to the GT: the exp(-0.6017/T) term is crucial. Very few candidates have `exp(c/T)`. Let me search systematically:

- Candidate 34: has `exp(c8/T)` but not multiplied by epsilon**(1/5)
- No other candidate seems to have `exp(c/T)`.

Most candidates have `exp(T*c)` which is fundamentally different from `exp(c/T)`.

Wait - can any structure approximate `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T)`? If c/T is small, `exp(-c/T) ≈ 1 - c/T + ...`. So `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T) ≈ epsilon**0.2 - c*epsilon**0.2/T + ...`

**Candidate 15:** `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c1 + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*exp(c4*epsilon**(1/3)) + c5*epsilon**(1/5) + c6*exp(T*c7) + c8*epsilon**(1/5)/T`

This has `c5*epsilon**(1/5) + c8*epsilon**(1/5)/T = epsilon**(1/5)*(c5 + c8/T)`. With c/T ≈ 0.6017/T being small, the first-order Taylor expansion `71.356*epsilon**0.2*(1 - 0.6017/T) ≈ 71.356*epsilon**0.2 - 42.93*epsilon**0.2/T` could be approximated. But this is only an approximation, not exact equivalence.

Since `exp(-c/T) ≠ (a + b/T)` for any constants, this isn't exact.

After thorough analysis, none of the candidates can produce the exact `epsilon**(~0.2) * exp(-const/T)` term that appears in the GT. No candidate has a term combining a power of epsilon with `exp(c/T)`.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `2.097*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T) + 3.305*epsilon**3*(T - 370.17)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `2.097*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T) + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 - 1223.4*epsilon**3`
- `= 3.305*T*epsilon**3 + (2.097 - 1223.4)*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`
- `= 3.305*T*epsilon**3 - 1221.3*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`

So GT has three structural terms:
1. **T·epsilon³** (linear in T times epsilon³)
2. **epsilon³** (constant times epsilon³)
3. **epsilon^0.2 · exp(-0.6018/T)** (epsilon^(1/5) times exp(negative/T))

Note: c3 ≈ 0.2 ≈ 1/5, so epsilon^c3 ≈ epsilon^(1/5).

The key term is `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(-c/T)`. This is NOT the same as:
- `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(c*T)` — exponential in T vs exponential in -1/T
- `exp(c/T)` without epsilon dependence
- Various other forms

Let me check which candidates can produce `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(-c/T)`.

Most candidates have `exp(T*c)` instead of `exp(c/T)` — these are fundamentally different functions and cannot match.

Let me carefully check each candidate for the ability to produce the term `epsilon^0.2 * exp(-c/T)`:

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c1*epsilon**(1/5) + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4*epsilon**(1/3)*exp(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*exp(c8/T) + c9/T`

This has `exp(c8/T)` but NOT multiplied by `epsilon^(1/5)`. The epsilon^(1/5) term is separate (`c1*epsilon**(1/5)`). So we'd need `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(-c/T)` but this candidate has them as separate additive terms. Cannot match.

Going through all candidates systematically, I need to find one with the term structure `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(something/T)` or equivalent.

None of the candidates contain `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(c/T)` as a product. The closest structures involve `exp(T*c)` (exponential in T, not 1/T), or `exp(c*epsilon)` terms.

Let me verify: `exp(-c4/(c5*T))` with c4=5.003, c5=8.314 gives `exp(-0.6018/T)`. This is NOT equivalent to `exp(c*T)` for any constant c. These are fundamentally different functions of T.

No candidate has the functional form `epsilon^(~0.2) * exp(const/T)`. The exponential dependence on 1/T (Arrhenius-type) cannot be replicated by `exp(c*T)`, polynomial terms in T, `1/T`, `1/T²`, `sqrt(T)`, `T^c`, `log(...)`, or any other structure present in the candidates.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can produce the required `epsilon^(1/5) * exp(-c/T)` term.
